**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

- Use `github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |

| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Implement RateLimitMiddleware for Django

## Objective
Create a new `RateLimitMiddleware` class in `django/middleware/ratelimit.py` that provides
configurable per-IP request rate limiting using Django's cache framework.

## Requirements

1. **Create `django/middleware/ratelimit.py`** with a `RateLimitMiddleware` class that:
   - Inherits from `MiddlewareMixin` (see `django/utils/deprecation.py`)
   - Reads configuration from `settings.RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS` (default: 100) and `settings.RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW` (default: 3600 seconds)
   - Uses Django's cache framework (`django.core.cache.cache`) to track request counts per IP
   - Returns `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` (429) when limit is exceeded
   - Implements `process_request(self, request)` following the middleware pattern

2. **Update `django/http/__init__.py`** to export `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` if not already present

3. **Create `tests/middleware/test_ratelimit.py`** with test cases for:
   - Normal requests within limit
   - Requests exceeding limit
   - Cache key isolation per IP
   - Custom settings override

## Key Reference Files
- `django/middleware/csrf.py` — middleware pattern with `process_request`/`process_view`
- `django/middleware/common.py` — middleware using settings and returning responses
- `django/utils/deprecation.py` — `MiddlewareMixin` base class
- `django/core/cache/__init__.py` — cache framework API
- `django/http/response.py` — HTTP response classes (HttpResponseForbidden, etc.)

## Success Criteria
- RateLimitMiddleware class exists and follows Django middleware conventions
- Uses cache framework for rate tracking (not in-memory dict)
- Returns 429 status code when rate limit exceeded
- Has proper imports from django.conf, django.core.cache, django.http
- Test file exists with JUnit-style test methods

    14→class RateLimitMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):
    15→    """
    16→    Middleware that enforces rate limiting per IP address.
    17→
    18→    Uses Django's cache framework to track request counts.
    19→    Returns 429 (Too Many Requests) when the limit is exceeded.
    20→    """
    21→
    22→    def process_request(self, request):
    23→        """
    24→        Check if the request IP has exceeded the rate limit.
    25→
    26→        Returns HttpResponseTooManyRequests if limit is exceeded, None otherwise.
    27→        """
    28→        # Get configuration from settings with defaults
    29→        rate_limit_requests = getattr(settings, "RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS", 100)
    30→        rate_limit_window = getattr(settings, "RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW", 3600)
    31→
    32→        # Get client IP address
    33→        client_ip = request.META.get("REMOTE_ADDR", "")
    34→
    35→        # Create cache key for this IP
    36→        cache_key = f"ratelimit:{client_ip}"
    37→
    38→        # Get current request count from cache
    39→        current_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)
    40→
    41→        # Check if limit exceeded
    42→        if current_count >= rate_limit_requests:
    43→            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()
    44→
    45→        # Increment request count
    46→        cache.set(cache_key, curre

178-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully implemented the RateLimitMiddleware for Django. Here's a summary of what was created:

## Implementation Summary

### 1. **Created `django/middleware/ratelimit.py`**
   - `RateLimitMiddleware` class that inherits from `MiddlewareMixin`
   - Implements `process_request()` method that:
     - Reads configuration from `settings.RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS` (default: 100) and `settings.RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW` (default: 3600 seconds)
     - Uses Django's cache framework to track request counts per IP address
     - Returns `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` (429) when limit is exceeded
     - Properly increments the cache counter for each request within the limit

### 2. **Updated `django/http/response.py`**
   - Added `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` class with `status_code = 429`
   - Placed between `HttpResponseGone` (410) and `HttpResponseServerError` (500)

### 3. **Updated `django/http/__init__.py`**
   - Added import for `HttpResponseTooManyRequests`
   - Added it to `__all__` export list

### 4. **Created `tests/middleware/test_ratelimit.py`**
   - Comprehensive test suite with 7 test methods:
     - `test_normal_requests_within_limit()` - Verifies requests within limit pass through
     - `test_requests_exceeding_limit()` - Verifies 429 response on limit exceeded
     - `test_cache_key_isolation_per_ip()` - Verifies per-IP rate limiting isolation
     - `test_custom_settings_override()` - Verifies custom settings work
     - `test_missing_remote_addr()` - Handles missing REMOTE_ADDR gracefully
     - `test_rate_limit_response_is_429()` - Verifies correct status code
     - `test_default_settings()` - Verifies defaults work correctly

### 5. **Fixed Python 3.10 Compatibility Issues**
   - Updated `django/utils/version.py` to handle `datetime.UTC` (Python 3.11+)

  "content": "\"\"\"\nRate limiting middleware for Django.\n\nThis module provides a middleware that limits the number of requests\nfrom a single IP address within a specified time window.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom django.conf import settings\nfrom django.core.cache import cache\nfrom django.http import HttpResponseTooManyRequests\nfrom django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin\n\n\nclass RateLimitMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Middleware that enforces rate limiting per IP address.\n\n    Uses Django's cache framework to track request counts.\n    Returns 429 (Too Many Requests) when the limit is exceeded.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def process_request(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Check if the request IP has exceeded the rate limit.\n\n        Returns HttpResponseTooManyRequests if limit is exceeded, None otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Get configuration from settings with defaults\n        rate_limit_requests = getattr(settings, \"RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS\", 100)\n        rate_limit_window = getattr(settings, \"RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW\", 3600)\n\n        # Get client IP address\n        client_ip = request.META.get(\"REMOTE_ADDR\", \"\")\n\n        # Create cache key for this IP\n        cache_key = f\"ratelimit:{client_ip}\"\n\n        # Get current request count from cache\n        current_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)\n\n        # Check if limit exceeded\n        if current_count >= rate_limit_requests:\n            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()\n\n        # Increment request count\n        cache.set(cache_key, current_count + 1, rate_limit_window)\n\n        return None\n",

  "content": "from django.core.cache import cache\nfrom django.http import HttpResponse, HttpResponseTooManyRequests\nfrom django.middleware.ratelimit import RateLimitMiddleware\nfrom django.test import RequestFactory, SimpleTestCase, override_settings\n\n\ndef get_response(request):\n    \"\"\"Simple response for middleware testing.\"\"\"\n    return HttpResponse(\"OK\")\n\n\nclass RateLimitMiddlewareTests(SimpleTestCase):\n    \"\"\"Tests for RateLimitMiddleware.\"\"\"\n\n    def setUp(self):\n        self.factory = RequestFactory()\n        # Clear cache before each test\n        cache.clear()\n\n    def tearDown(self):\n        # Clear cache after each test\n        cache.clear()\n\n    def test_normal_requests_within_limit(self):\n        \"\"\"Requests within the limit should pass through normally.\"\"\"\n        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n        request = self.factory.get(\"/test/\")\n        request.META[\"REMOTE_ADDR\"] = \"127.0.0.1\"\n\n        # Make several requests within the default limit (100)\n        for _ in range(50):\n            response = middleware(request)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n            self.assertEqual(response.content, b\"OK\")\n\n    def test_requests_exceeding_limit(self):\n        \"\"\"Requests exceeding the limit should return 429.\"\"\"\n        with override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=3, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600):\n            middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n            request = self.factory.get(\"/test/\")\n            request.META[\"REMOTE_ADDR\"] = \"127.0.0.1\"\n\n            # First 3 requests should succeed\n            for i in range(3):\n                response = middleware(request)\n                self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n\n            # 4th request should be rate limited\n            response = middleware(request)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 429)\n            self.assertIsInstance(response, HttpResponseTooManyRequests)\n\n    def test_cache_key_isolation_per_ip(self):\n        \"\"\"Different IPs should have separate request counts.\"\"\"\n        with override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=2, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600):\n            middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n\n            # First IP makes 2 requests\n            request1 = self.factory.get(\"/test/\")\n            request1.META[\"REMOTE_ADDR\"] = \"192.168.1.1\"\n            response = middleware(request1)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n            response = middleware(request1)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n\n            # Second IP should have its own limit\n            request2 = self.factory.get(\"/test/\")\n            request2.META[\"REMOTE_ADDR\"] = \"192.168.1.2\"\n            response = middleware(request2)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n            response = middleware(request2)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n\n            # Third request from first IP should be rate limited\n            response = middleware(request1)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 429)\n\n            # But third request from second IP should also be rate limited\n            response = middleware(request2)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 429)\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=5, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)\n    def test_custom_settings_override(self):\n        \"\"\"Custom settings should override defaults.\"\"\"\n        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n        request = self.factory.get(\"/test/\")\n        request.META[\"REMOTE_ADDR\"] = \"127.0.0.1\"\n\n        # Should allow up to 5 requests\n        for i in range(5):\n            response = middleware(request)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n\n        # 6th request should be rate limited\n        response = middleware(request)\n        self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 429)\n\n    def test_missing_remote_addr(self):\n        \"\"\"Middleware should handle missing REMOTE_ADDR gracefully.\"\"\"\n        with override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=2, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600):\n            middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n            request = self.factory.get(\"/test/\")\n            # Don't set REMOTE_ADDR\n\n            # Should not raise an error and should work with empty IP\n            response = middleware(request)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n\n            response = middleware(request)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n\n            # Third request with empty IP should be rate limited\n            response = middleware(request)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 429)\n\n    def test_rate_limit_response_is_429(self):\n        \"\"\"Rate limit response should have status code 429.\"\"\"\n        with override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=1, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600):\n            middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n            request = self.factory.get(\"/test/\")\n            request.META[\"REMOTE_ADDR\"] = \"127.0.0.1\"\n\n            # First request is OK\n            response = middleware(request)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n\n            # Second request is rate limited\n            response = middleware(request)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 429)\n\n    def test_default_settings(self):\n        \"\"\"Middleware should use default settings when not configured.\"\"\"\n        # Use default settings (100 requests per 3600 seconds)\n        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response)\n        request = self.factory.get(\"/test/\")\n        request.META[\"REMOTE_ADDR\"] = \"127.0.0.1\"\n\n        # Should allow 100 requests by default\n        for i in range(100):\n            response = middleware(request)\n            self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 200)\n\n        # 101st request should be rate limited\n        response = middleware(request)\n        self.assertEqual(response.status_code, 429)\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/django/middleware/ratelimit.py
"""
Rate limiting middleware for Django.

This module provides a middleware that limits the number of requests
from a single IP address within a specified time window.
"""

from django.conf import settings
from django.core.cache import cache
from django.http import HttpResponseTooManyRequests
from django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin


class RateLimitMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):
    """
    Middleware that enforces rate limiting per IP address.

    Uses Django's cache framework to track request counts.
    Returns 429 (Too Many Requests) when the limit is exceeded.
    """

    def process_request(self, request):
        """
        Check if the request IP has exceeded the rate limit.

        Returns HttpResponseTooManyRequests if limit is exceeded, None otherwise.
        """
        # Get configuration from settings with defaults
        rate_limit_requests = getattr(settings, "RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS", 100)
        rate_limit_window = getattr(settings, "RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW", 3600)

        # Get client IP address
        client_ip = request.META.get("REMOTE_ADDR", "")

        # Create cache key for this IP
        cache_key = f"ratelimit:{client_ip}"

        # Get current request count from cache
        current_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)

        # Check if limit exceeded
        if current_count >= rate_limit_requests:
            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()

        # Increment request count
        cache.set(cache_key, current_count + 1, rate_limit_window)

        return None

    def __init__(self, data):
        """
        Populate the initial data using __setitem__ to ensure values are
        correctly encoded.

        self._store = {}

            for header, value in self._unpack_items(data):
                self[header] = value

        """

10. WRITE /workspace/django/middleware/ratelimit.py
"""
Rate limiting middleware for Django.

This module provides a middleware that limits the number of requests
from a single IP address within a specified time window.
"""

from django.conf import settings
from django.core.cache import cache
from django.http import HttpResponseTooManyRequests
from django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin


class RateLimitMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):
    """
    Middleware that enforces rate limiting per IP address.

    Uses Django's cache framework to track request counts.
    Returns 429 (Too Many Requests) when the limit is exceeded.
    """

    def process_request(self, request):
        """
        Check if the request IP has exceeded the rate limit.

        Returns HttpResponseTooManyRequests if limit is exceeded, None otherwise.
        """
        # Get configuration from settings with defaults
        rate_limit_requests = getattr(settings, "RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS", 100)
        rate_limit_window = getattr(settings, "RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW", 3600)

        # Get client IP address
        client_ip = request.META.get("REMOTE_ADDR", "")

        # Create cache key for this IP
        cache_key = f"ratelimit:{client_ip}"

        # Get current request count from cache
        current_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)

        # Check if limit exceeded
        if current_count >= rate_limit_requests:
            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests()

        # Increment request count
        cache.set(cache_key, current_count + 1, rate_limit_window)

        return None

        self.cookies[key] = value

            if isinstance(expires, datetime.datetime):

After
        self.cookies[key] = value
        if expires is not None:
            if isinstance(expires, datetime.datetime):
                utc = datetime.UTC if hasattr(datetime, 'UTC') else datetime.timezone.utc
                if timezone.is_naive(expires):
                    expires = timezone.make_aware(expires, utc)
                delta = expires - datetime.datetime.now(tz=utc)

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace')

# Test imports
try:
    from django.http import HttpResponseTooManyRequests
    print("✓ HttpResponseTooManyRequests imported successfully")
    print(f"  Status code: {HttpResponseTooManyRequests.status_code}")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"✗ Failed to import HttpResponseTooManyRequests: {e}")
    sys.exit(1)

try:
    from django.middleware.ratelimit import RateLimitMiddleware
    print("✓ RateLimitMiddleware imported successfully")
    
    # Verify it's a proper middleware
    from django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin
    print(f"  Inherits from MiddlewareMixin: {issubclass(RateLimitMiddleware, MiddlewareMixin)}")
    print(f"  Has process_request: {hasattr(RateLimitMiddleware, 'process_request')}")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"✗ Failed to import RateLimitMiddleware: {e}")
    sys.exit(1)

print("\nAll imports successful!")
